}
15/02/23, 10:44โฏam - Guneet Kaur: The code first initializes an array of process names and an array of their respective burst times. It then calculates the waiting time for each process using the FCFS algorithm. The waiting time for the first process is always 0, and the waiting time for subsequent processes is the sum of the burst times of all previous processes. Finally, the code prints the waiting times for each process.

15/02/23, 10:56โฏam - Guneet Kaur: Here's an implementation of FCFS scheduling algorithm in C++ to handle a given order of processes p1, p2, and p3 with CPU burst time of 24, 3, 3 and order of arrival of 3, 1, 2.

To calculate the average waiting time, we will first sort the processes based on their order of arrival using bubble sort, then we will calculate the waiting time for each process by subtracting the arrival time from the completion time of the previous process (or 0 for the first process). Finally, we will calculate the average waiting time by summing up all waiting times and dividing by the total number of processes.

c
Copy code
#include <iostream>
#include <algorithm>

using namespace std;

// Process structure to store process information
struct Process {
    int id;
    int arrivalTime;
    int burstTime;
};

int main() {
    // Define the three processes
    Process p1 = {1, 3, 24};
    Process p2 = {2, 1, 3};
    Process p3 = {3, 2, 3};

    // Sort the processes based on their arrival time using bubble sort
    Process processes[] = {p1, p2, p3};
    int n = 3;
    for (int i = 0; i < n - 1; i++) {
        for (int j = 0; j < n - i - 1; j++) {
            if (processes[j].arrivalTime > processes[j+1].arrivalTime) {
                swap(processes[j], processes[j+1]);
            }
        }
    }

    // Calculate the completion time and waiting time for each process
    int completionTime = processes[0].burstTime;
    int totalWaitingTime = 0;
    for (int i = 1; i < n; i++) {
        completionTime += processes[i].burstTime;
        int waitingTime = completionTime - processes[i].arrivalTime - processes[i].burstTime;
        totalWaitingTime += max(waitingTime, 0); // waiting time cannot be negative
    }

    // Calculate and print the average waiting time
    double avgWaitingTime = static_cast<double>(totalWaitingTime) / n;
    cout << "Average waiting time: " << avgWaitingTime << endl;

    return 0;
}
This code should output the average waiting time of the three processes after sorting them by their arrival time using bubble sort.

23/02/23, 11:36โฏam - Guneet Kaur: Here is the code to implement the Shortest Job First (SJF) algorithm in C++ for the given set of processes:

#include <iostream>
#include <algorithm>

using namespace std;

// Process structure
struct Process {
    int id;
    int burstTime;
};

// Function to compare processes based on burst time
bool compareProcesses(Process p1, Process p2) {
    return p1.burstTime < p2.burstTime;
}

int main() {
    // Create an array of processes
    Process processes[] = {{1, 24}, {2, 3}, {3, 3}};
    int n = sizeof(processes) / sizeof(processes[0]);

    // Sort the processes based on burst time
    sort(processes, processes + n, compareProcesses);

    // Initialize waiting time and total waiting time
    int waitingTime[n], totalWaitingTime = 0;
    waitingTime[0] = 0;

    // Calculate waiting time for each process
    for (int i = 1; i < n; i++) {
        waitingTime[i] = waitingTime[i-1] + processes[i-1].burstTime;
        totalWaitingTime += waitingTime[i];
    }

    // Calculate average waiting time
    double avgWaitingTime = (double)totalWaitingTime / n;

    // Print the waiting time and average waiting time
    cout << "Process\tBurst Time\tWaiting Time\n";
    for (int i = 0; i < n; i++) {
        cout << "P" << processes[i].id << "\t" << processes[i].burstTime << "\t\t" << waitingTime[i] << "\n";
    }
    cout << "Average Waiting Time: " << avgWaitingTime << "\n";

    return 0;
}
The above code sorts the given set of processes based on their burst time in ascending order. Then, it calculates the waiting time for each process using the formula waitingTime[i] = waitingTime[i-1] + processes[i-1].burstTime. Finally, it prints the waiting time and the average waiting time for the set of processes.

For the given set of processes {P1, P2, P3} with burst time {24, 3, 3}, the output of the code will be:

css
Copy code
Process  Burst Time  Waiting Time
P2       3           0
P3       3           3
P1       24          6
Average Waiting Time: 3
Therefore, the average waiting time for the given set of processes is 3.
23/02/23, 11:36โฏam - Guneet Kaur: write a code to implement priority scheduling in c++ with processes p1, p2 , p3 ,p4, p5 with  priority number 9, 1, 2, 1, 5 respectively and burst time 3, 1, 4, 5, 2 with shortest job first 
Here's an implementation of priority scheduling with shortest job first in C++:
#include <iostream>
#include <queue>
#include <vector>
using namespace std;

// process structure
struct process {
    int id; // process id
    int priority; // priority number
    int burst_time; // burst time

    // constructor
    process(int id, int priority, int burst_time)
        : id(id), priority(priority), burst_time(burst_time) {}

    // overloaded comparison operator for priority queue
    bool operator<(const process& p) const {
        return priority > p.priority || (priority == p.priority && burst_time > p.burst_time);
    }
};

// main function
int main() {
    // create processes
    process p1(1, 9, 3);
    process p2(2, 1, 1);
    process p3(3, 2, 4);
    process p4(4, 1, 5);
    process p5(5, 5, 2);

    // create priority queue for processes
    priority_queue<process> pq;

    // add processes to priority queue
    pq.push(p1);
    pq.push(p2);
    pq.push(p3);
    pq.push(p4);
    pq.push(p5);

    // process priority queue
    while (!pq.empty()) {
        process p = pq.top(); // get process with highest priority
        pq.pop(); // remove process from priority queue
        cout << "Processing process " << p.id << " with priority " << p.priority << " and burst time " << p.burst_time << endl;
        // process the job here
    }

    return 0;
}
The code creates a priority queue of processes and uses an overloaded comparison operator to prioritize processes based on their priority number and burst time. The while loop processes the highest priority process in the queue and removes it from the queue until the queue is empty. Note that the actual processing of the job is left as an exercise for the reader, as it depends on the specific requirements of the problem.

18/04/23, 4:46โฏpm - Gurleen Kaur: #include <iostream>
#include <vector>
#include <queue>
#include <algorithm>

using namespace std;

// Process structure to store information about a process
struct Process {
    int id;
    int arrival_time;
    int burst_time;
    int remaining_time;
};

// Comparison function for the priority queue
struct Compare {
    bool operator() (const Process& p1, const Process& p2) {
        return p1.remaining_time > p2.remaining_time;
    }
};

int main() {
    int n; // number of processes
    cout << "Enter the number of processes: ";
    cin >> n;

    vector<Process> processes(n);
    cout << "Enter the arrival time and burst time of each process:\n";
    for (int i = 0; i < n; i++) {
        processes[i].id = i+1;
        cin >> processes[i].arrival_time >> processes[i].burst_time;
        processes[i].remaining_time = processes[i].burst_time;
    }

    // Sort processes by arrival time
    sort(processes.begin(), processes.end(), [](const Process& p1, const Process& p2) {
        return p1.arrival_time < p2.arrival_time;
    });

    priority_queue<Process, vector<Process>, Compare> pq; // priority queue for SJF with preemption
    int current_time = 0; // current time
    int completed = 0; // number of completed processes
    double total_waiting_time = 0; // total waiting time of all processes

    // Loop until all processes are completed
    while (completed < n) {
        // Add processes that have arrived to the priority queue
        for (int i = 0; i < n; i++) {
            if (processes[i].arrival_time <= current_time && processes[i].remaining_time > 0) {
                pq.push(processes[i]);
            }
        }

        if (!pq.empty()) {
            Process current_process = pq.top(); // get the process with the shortest remaining time
            pq.pop();

            // Update waiting time and remaining time of the current process
            total_waiting_time += current_time - current_process.arrival_time;
            current_time += min(current_process.remaining_time, 1); // execute the process for 1 unit of time
            current_process.remaining_time -= 1;

            // Add the current process back to the priority queue if it still has remaining time
            if (current_process.remaining_time > 0) {
                pq.push(current_process);
            }
            else {
                completed += 1; // process is completed
                cout << "Process " << current_process.id << " completed at time " << current_time << endl;
            }
        }
        else {
            current_time++; // no processes to execute, just increase the time
        }
    }

    double average_waiting_time = total_waiting_time / n;
    cout << "Average waiting time: " << average_waiting_time << endl;

    return 0;
}
18/04/23, 4:46โฏpm - Gurleen Kaur: #include <iostream>
#include <queue>
using namespace std;

struct Process {
    int pid; // process ID
    int bt; // burst time
};

void roundRobin(Process processes[], int n, int quantum) {
    queue<int> q;
    int wt[n], tat[n], total_wt = 0, total_tat = 0;

    // Enqueue all processes
    for (int i = 0; i < n; i++) {
        q.push(i);
        wt[i] = 0; // initialize wait time to 0
    }

    // Process each job in queue
    while (!q.empty()) {
        int i = q.front();
        q.pop();

        if (processes[i].bt <= quantum) {
            // Process finishes within quantum
            tat[i] = processes[i].bt + wt[i];
            total_tat += tat[i];
            total_wt += wt[i] + quantum - processes[i].bt;
            processes[i].bt = 0;
        }
        else {
            // Process still needs more time
            processes[i].bt -= quantum;
            total_wt += quantum;
            q.push(i);
        }
    }

    // Print results
    cout << "PID\tBT\tWT\tTAT\n";
    for (int i = 0; i < n; i++) {
        cout << processes[i].pid << "\t"
            << processes[i].bt << "\t"
            << wt[i] << "\t"
            << tat[i] << endl;
    }
    cout << "Average waiting time: " << (float)total_wt / (float)n << endl;
    cout << "Average turnaround time: " << (float)total_tat / (float)n << endl;
}

int main() {
    int n, quantum;
    cout << "Enter number of processes: ";
    cin >> n;
    Process processes[n];

    // Input process details
    for (int i = 0; i < n; i++) {
        processes[i].pid = i;
        cout << "Enter burst time for process " << i << ": ";
        cin >> processes[i].bt;
    }

    // Input time quantum
    cout << "Enter time quantum: ";
    cin >> quantum;

    // Run round robin scheduling algorithm
    roundRobin(processes, n, quantum);

    return 0;
}

30/04/23, 10:03โฏpm - Guneet Kaur: #include <bits/stdc++.h>
using namespace std;
int turnAroundTime(int processes[], int n, int bt[], int wt[], int tat[])
{
    for (int i = 0; i < n; i++)
        tat[i] = bt[i] + wt[i];
    return 1;
}

int waitingTime(int processes[], int n, int bt[], int wt[], int quantum)
{
    int rem_bt[n];
    for (int i = 0; i < n; i++)
        rem_bt[i] = bt[i];
    int t = 0; // total time takes to cmmplete job

    while (1)
    {
        bool done = true;

        for (int i = 0; i < n; i++)
        {
            if (rem_bt[i] > 0)
            {
                done = false;
                if (rem_bt[i] > quantum)
                {
                    t += quantum;
                    rem_bt[i] -= quantum;
                }
                else
                {
                    t = t + rem_bt[i];
                    wt[i] = t - bt[i];
                    rem_bt[i] = 0;
                }
            }
        }
        if (done == true)
            break;
    }

    return 1;
}

int findavgTime(int processes[], int n, int bt[], int quantum)
{
    int wt[n], tat[n], total_wt = 0, total_tat = 0;
    waitingTime(processes, n, bt, wt, quantum);
    turnAroundTime(processes, n, bt, wt, tat);

    cout << "process burstTime waitingTime TurnAroundTime\n";

    for (int i = 0; i < n; i++)
    {
        total_wt = total_wt + wt[i];
        total_tat = total_tat + tat[i];
        cout << "\t" << i + 1 << "\t\t\t" << bt[i] << "\t\t\t" << wt[i] << "\t\t\t" << tat[i] << endl;
    }

    cout << "average waiting time =" << (float)total_wt / (float)n << endl;
    cout << "average turnaround time =" << (float)total_tat / (float)n << endl;

    return 1;
}
int main()
{
    int processes[] = {1, 2, 3};
    int n = sizeof(processes) / sizeof(processes[0]);
    int burst_time[] = {8, 6, 12};

    int quantum = 2;
    findavgTime(processes, n, burst_time, quantum);
    return 0;
}

30/04/23, 10:15โฏpm - Guneet Kaur: // C++ program to implement Shortest Remaining Time First
// Shortest Remaining Time First (SRTF)

#include <bits/stdc++.h>
using namespace std;

struct Process {
	int pid; // Process ID
	int bt; // Burst Time
	int art; // Arrival Time
};

// Function to find the waiting time for all
// processes
void findWaitingTime(Process proc[], int n,
								int wt[])
{
	int rt[n];

	// Copy the burst time into rt[]
	for (int i = 0; i < n; i++)
		rt[i] = proc[i].bt;

	int complete = 0, t = 0, minm = INT_MAX;
	int shortest = 0, finish_time;
	bool check = false;

	// Process until all processes gets
	// completed
	while (complete != n) {

		// Find process with minimum
		// remaining time among the
		// processes that arrives till the
		// current time`
		for (int j = 0; j < n; j++) {
			if ((proc[j].art <= t) &&
			(rt[j] < minm) && rt[j] > 0) {
				minm = rt[j];
				shortest = j;
				check = true;
			}
		}

		if (check == false) {
			t++;
			continue;
		}

		// Reduce remaining time by one
		rt[shortest]--;

		// Update minimum
		minm = rt[shortest];
		if (minm == 0)
			minm = INT_MAX;

		// If a process gets completely
		// executed
		if (rt[shortest] == 0) {

			// Increment complete
			complete++;
			check = false;

			// Find finish time of current
			// process
			finish_time = t + 1;

			// Calculate waiting time
			wt[shortest] = finish_time -
						proc[shortest].bt -
						proc[shortest].art;

			if (wt[shortest] < 0)
				wt[shortest] = 0;
		}
		// Increment time
		t++;
	}
}

// Function to calculate turn around time
void findTurnAroundTime(Process proc[], int n,
						int wt[], int tat[])
{
	// calculating turnaround time by adding
	// bt[i] + wt[i]
	for (int i = 0; i < n; i++)
		tat[i] = proc[i].bt + wt[i];
}

// Function to calculate average time
void findavgTime(Process proc[], int n)
{
	int wt[n], tat[n], total_wt = 0,
					total_tat = 0;

	// Function to find waiting time of all
	// processes
	findWaitingTime(proc, n, wt);

	// Function to find turn around time for
	// all processes
	findTurnAroundTime(proc, n, wt, tat);

	// Display processes along with all
	// details
	cout << " P\t\t"
		<< "BT\t\t"
		<< "WT\t\t"
		<< "TAT\t\t\n";

	// Calculate total waiting time and
	// total turnaround time
	for (int i = 0; i < n; i++) {
		total_wt = total_wt + wt[i];
		total_tat = total_tat + tat[i];
		cout << " " << proc[i].pid << "\t\t"
			<< proc[i].bt << "\t\t " << wt[i]
			<< "\t\t " << tat[i] << endl;
	}

	cout << "\nAverage waiting time = "
		<< (float)total_wt / (float)n;
	cout << "\nAverage turn around time = "
		<< (float)total_tat / (float)n;
}

// Driver code
int main()
{
	Process proc[] = { { 1, 6, 2 }, { 2, 2, 5 },
					{ 3, 8, 1 }, { 4, 3, 0}, {5, 4, 4} };
	int n = sizeof(proc) / sizeof(proc[0]);

	findavgTime(proc, n);
	return 0;
}

struct Process {
	int pid; // Process ID

	int art; // Arrival Time

// Function to find the waiting time for all
// processes
void findWaitingTime(Process proc[], int n,
								int wt[])
{
	int rt[n];

	// Copy the burst time into rt[]
	for (int i = 0; i < n; i++)
		rt[i] = proc[i].bt;

	int complete = 0, t = 0, minm = INT_MAX;
	int shortest = 0, finish_time;
	bool check = false;

	// Process until all processes gets
	// completed
	while (complete != n) {

		// Find process with minimum
		// remaining time among the
		// processes that arrives till the
		// current time`
		for (int j = 0; j < n; j++) {
			if ((proc[j].art <= t) &&
			(rt[j] < minm) && rt[j] > 0) {
				minm = rt[j];
				shortest = j;
				check = true;
			}
		}

		if (check == false) {
			t++;
			continue;
		}

		// Reduce remaining time by one
		rt[shortest]--;

		// Update minimum
		minm = rt[shortest];
		if (minm == 0)
			minm = INT_MAX;

		// If a process gets completely
		// executed
		if (rt[shortest] == 0) {

			// Increment complete
			complete++;
			check = false;

			// Find finish time of current
			// process
			finish_time = t + 1;

			// Calculate waiting time
			wt[shortest] = finish_time -
						proc[shortest].bt -
						proc[shortest].art;

			if (wt[shortest] < 0)
				wt[shortest] = 0;
		}
		// Increment time
		t++;
	}
}

// Function to calculate turn around time
void findTurnAroundTime(Process proc[], int n,
						int wt[], int tat[])
{
	// calculating turnaround time by adding
	// bt[i] + wt[i]
	for (int i = 0; i < n; i++)
		tat[i] = proc[i].bt + wt[i];
}

// Function to calculate average time
void findavgTime(Process proc[], int n)
{
	int wt[n], tat[n], total_wt = 0,
					total_tat = 0;

	// Function to find waiting time of all
	// processes
	findWaitingTime(proc, n, wt);

	// Function to find turn around time for
	// all processes
	findTurnAroundTime(proc, n, wt, tat);

	// Display processes along with all
	// details
	cout << " P\t\t"
		<< "BT\t\t"
		<< "WT\t\t"
		<< "TAT\t\t\n";

	// Calculate total waiting time and
	// total turnaround time
	for (int i = 0; i < n; i++) {
		total_wt = total_wt + wt[i];
		total_tat = total_tat + tat[i];
		cout << " " << proc[i].pid << "\t\t"
			<< proc[i].bt << "\t\t " << wt[i]
			<< "\t\t " << tat[i] << endl;
	}

	cout << "\nAverage waiting time = "
		<< (float)total_wt / (float)n;
	cout << "\nAverage turn around time = "
		<< (float)total_tat / (float)n;
}

// Driver code
int main()
{
	Process proc[] = { { 1, 6, 2 }, { 2, 2, 5 },
					{ 3, 8, 1 }, { 4, 3, 0}, {5, 4, 4} };
	int n = sizeof(proc) / sizeof(proc[0]);

	findavgTime(proc, n);
	return 0;
}

12/09/23, 5:50โฏpm - Guneet Kaur: In theoretical computer science and the study of formal languages in the context of Theory of Computation (ToC), the "closeness properties" of language classes refer to certain characteristics that define how languages within a class relate to each other. Here are some common closeness properties associated with language classes:

1. Closure under Union: A language class is said to have the closure under union property if, when you take the union of two languages from that class, the result is still within that class. For example, if two context-free languages are combined using union, the resulting language is also context-free.

2. Closure under Intersection: This property means that if you take the intersection of two languages from a class, the result is still in the same class. For example, if two regular languages are intersected, the resulting language is also regular.

3. Closure under Complement: A language class exhibits this property if the complement of a language from that class is also in the same class. Regular languages are closed under complement, which means that if a language is regular, its complement is also regular.

4. Closure under Concatenation: This property implies that if you concatenate (or "join") two languages from a class, the resulting language is still in that class. Context-free languages are closed under concatenation.

5. Closure under Kleene Star: A language class has this property if the Kleene star operation (closure under repetition) on a language from the class results in a language within the same class. Regular languages have this property.

6. Closure under Homomorphism: This property states that if you apply a homomorphism (a function that maps one alphabet to another) to a language in the class, the resulting language remains in the same class. For example, context-free languages are closed under homomorphism.

These closeness properties are important for understanding the relationships between different language classes in formal language theory and are often used to prove theorems about the expressiveness and computational power of various language classes. They help in classifying languages and determining their computational complexity.

09/05/24, 9:10โฏpm - Guneet Kaur: Read this theory to Clear awt doubt
09/05/24, 9:15โฏpm - Guneet Kaur: The **AWT (Abstract Window Toolkit)** is an Application Programming Interface (API) in Java used for developing GUI (Graphical User Interfaces) or window-based applicationsยฒยณ. Here are some key points about the AWT package:

- It's part of the Java Foundation Classes (JFC) that provides a way to build platform-independent graphical applicationsยฒ.
- The `java.awt` package contains all of the classes for creating user interfaces and for painting graphics and imagesยนโต.
- A user interface object such as a button or a scrollbar is called, in AWT terminology, a component. The Component class is the root of all AWT componentsยนโต.
- AWT components are platform-dependent, which means they are shown in accordance with the operating systemโs viewยฒ.
- AWT is heavyweight, which means that its components consume resources from the underlying operating system (OS)ยฒ.
- The `java.awt` package contains AWT API classes such as TextField, Label, TextArea, RadioButton, CheckBox, Choice, List, and so onยฒ.
- AWT provides containers like panels, frames, and dialogues to organize and group components in the Applicationยฒ.
- Layout Managers are responsible for arranging data in the containers. Some of the layout managers are BorderLayout, FlowLayout, etcยฒ.

Despite the AWT components being platform dependent, AWT is considered platform independent because of the following reasonsยฒ:
1. JVM (Java Virtual Machine): As Java Virtual Machine is platform dependent.
2. Abstract APIs: AWT provides an abstract layer for GUI. Java applications interact with AWT through Abstract API which are platform independent. Abstract API allows Java to isolate platform-specific details, making code portable across different systems.
3. Platform-Independent Libraries: The Libraries of AWT are written in Java which they are totally platform-independent. Because of this, it ensures that AWT functionality remains consistent across different environments.

17/05/24, 10:13โฏpm - Guneet Kaur: Ada is a structured, statically typed, imperative, and object-oriented high-level programming language, inspired by Pascal and other languagesยน. Here are some of the main features of Ada programming:

1. *Strong Typing*: Ada has a strong typing system which helps in detecting errors at compile time rather than at runtimeยน.
Strongly Typed: In a strongly typed language like Ada, the type of a variable is known at compile time3
2. *Modular Programming Mechanisms (Packages)*: Ada supports modular programming through the use of packages. This allows for better organization and reusability of codeยน.
3. *Run-time Checking*: Ada includes built-in run-time checks to catch errors that might otherwise result in unpredictable behaviorยน.
4. *Parallel Processing*: Ada has built-in language support for parallel processing, including tasks, synchronous message passing, protected objects, and non-deterministic select statementsยน.
5. *Exception Handling*: Ada provides a mechanism for detecting and responding to exceptional run-time conditionsยน.
6. *Generics*: Ada supports generic programming, which allows for the definition of algorithms without specifying the exact data typesยน.
7. *Object-Oriented Programming*: Ada 95 added support for object-oriented programming, including dynamic dispatchยน.

These features make Ada a powerful language for developing complex, mission-critical systemsยน.
17/05/24, 10:13โฏpm - Guneet Kaur: Yes, the Ada programming language does support concurrencyยนยฒยณ. Here are some key points about Ada's concurrency features:

- *Tasks*: Ada has built-in support for concurrent programming through the use of tasksยนยฒ. A task in Ada is similar to a thread in other programming languages, but with more sophisticated and safer facilities for synchronization and communicationยฒ.
- *Protected Objects*: Protected objects in Ada serve as a building block to support other synchronization paradigmsยณ.
- *Real-Time Programming*: Ada's concurrency model is particularly suitable for real-time and embedded systems, like those found in aerospace applicationsยฒ.
- *Deterministic and Analyzable*: Adaโs concurrency support is carefully designed to be deterministic and analyzable, which are vital properties for high-integrity real-time systems often found in the aerospace domainยฒ.

These features make Ada a powerful language for developing complex, mission-critical systemsยนยฒ.

24/05/24, 7:51โฏpm - Guneet Kaur: panic mode
1The compiler examines each error entry in its parsing table (a data structure it uses to understand your code).
2 Based on language rules and patterns, it constructs a custom error-recovery routine. Think of it as a set of guidelines for fixing errors.
3 It fills in missing entries in the parsing table with pointers to these error-recovery procedures.

26/05/24, 3:27โฏpm - Guneet Kaur: panic mode
1 The compiler looks at the symbols in your code until it finds a specific symbol (letโs call it โaโ) that is part of a set of
allowed tokens
2. If it doesnโt find โaโ, it keeps skipping symbols until it does.
3 Once it finds โaโ, it shifts to a different state (a kind of internal representation) and continues checking your code. <This message was edited>

1 compiler examines each error entry in its parsing table (data structure it uses to understand code).

public class String2 {
  public static void main(String[] args) {
    Scanner sc = new Scanner (System.in);
    String original = sc.nextLine();
    String2 obj = new String2();

    for(int i= 0; i<original.length(); i++){
       if(original.charAt(i) == 'e'){
          obj.setCharAt('i');  
       }
  
    
    System.out.println("original :"+original);
    System.out.println("result: "+original);
  }  
}
}

23/10/24, 12:55โฏpm - Gurleen Kaur: class Solution {
    public int pivotIndex(int[] nums) {
     
       int totleSum=0;
       int leftSum=0;
       for(int num:nums){
        totleSum+=num;
       }
        
           for(int i=0;i<nums.length;i++){
              if(leftSum==totleSum-leftSum-nums[i]){
                return i;
              }
              leftSum+=nums[i];
           }
             
        
        return -1;
    }
}

24/10/24, 1:37โฏpm - Gurleen Kaur: class Solution {
    public List<List<Integer>> generate(int numRows) {
        List <List<Integer>> res=new ArrayList<List<Integer>>();
        List <Integer>rowpre=null;
        for(int i=0;i<numRows;++i){
            List<Integer> row=new ArrayList<Integer>();
            for(int j=0;j<=i;++j){
                if(j==0 || j==i){
                    row.add(1);
                }else{
                    row.add(rowpre.get(j-1)+rowpre.get(j));

ChatGPT said:
ChatGPT
Certainly! The code you provided generates Pascal's Triangle for a given number of rows, numRows. Let's break down the code step-by-step:

1. Class and Method Declaration:
java
Copy code
class Solution {
    public List<List<Integer>> generate(int numRows) {
You have a Solution class, which contains a public method called generate.
The generate method takes an integer numRows as an argument, which represents the number of rows to generate in Pascal's Triangle.
The return type of this method is List<List<Integer>>, which is a list of lists of integers (each list representing a row in Pascal's Triangle).
2. Initialize Variables:
java
Copy code
List<List<Integer>> res = new ArrayList<List<Integer>>();
List<Integer> rowpre = null;
res is a list that will store all the rows of Pascal's Triangle. It's initialized as an empty list of lists.
rowpre (short for "previous row") is a list that will hold the previous row's values while building the triangle. Itโs initialized as null.
3. Outer Loop - Iterating Over Rows:
java
Copy code
for (int i = 0; i < numRows; ++i) {
    List<Integer> row = new ArrayList<Integer>();
The outer for loop iterates from i = 0 to i < numRows, effectively generating each row one by one.
In each iteration, a new row list is created to store the current rowโs values.
4. Inner Loop - Filling Each Row:
java
Copy code
for (int j = 0; j <= i; ++j) {
    if (j == 0 || j == i) {
        row.add(1);
    } else {
        row.add(rowpre.get(j - 1) + rowpre.get(j));
    }
}
The inner for loop iterates from j = 0 to j <= i.
What does it do?
It constructs the current row (row) element by element.
Boundary Condition:
If j is 0 or i (first or last element of the row), it adds 1 to row.
Middle Elements:
If j is between 0 and i, it calculates the value based on the previous row (rowpre):
rowpre.get(j - 1) + rowpre.get(j) calculates the sum of the two numbers directly above the current position from the previous row.
This is the main rule of Pascal's Triangle.
5. Update Previous Row and Add Current Row to Result:
java
Copy code
rowpre = row;
res.add(row);
After finishing the current row:
rowpre is updated to reference the current row. This is so the next iteration can use the current row's values to generate the next row.
The completed row is added to the result list res.
6. Return the Result:
java
Copy code
return res;
    }
}
After the outer loop finishes generating all rows, the method returns the list res, which contains all the rows of Pascal's Triangle up to numRows.
Example Walkthrough:
Let's take an example with numRows = 5:

Iteration 1 (i = 0):

row = [1] โ (since it's the first element of the first row)
rowpre becomes [1].
res becomes [[1]].
Iteration 2 (i = 1):

row = [1, 1] โ (first and last element are 1)
rowpre becomes [1, 1].
res becomes [[1], [1, 1]].
Iteration 3 (i = 2):

row = [1, 2, 1] โ (middle element is 1 + 1 = 2)
rowpre becomes [1, 2, 1].
res becomes [[1], [1, 1], [1, 2, 1]].
Iteration 4 (i = 3):

row = [1, 3, 3, 1] โ (middle elements are 1+2 = 3 and 2+1 = 3)
rowpre becomes [1, 3, 3, 1].
res becomes [[1], [1, 1], [1, 2, 1], [1, 3, 3, 1]].
Iteration 5 (i = 4):

row = [1, 4, 6, 4, 1] โ (middle elements are 1+3 = 4, 3+3 = 6, and 3+1 = 4)
rowpre becomes [1, 4, 6, 4, 1].
res becomes [[1], [1, 1], [1, 2, 1], [1, 3, 3, 1], [1, 4, 6, 4, 1]].
Key Takeaways:
This code builds Pascal's Triangle row-by-row, using the previous rowโs values to calculate the next row.
It efficiently handles edge cases (first and last elements of each row) by directly assigning them as 1.
The time complexity is 
๐
(
๐
2
)
O(n 
2
 ) because it calculates each element exactly once.
Let me know if you need more clarification!
24/10/24, 1:38โฏpm - Gurleen Kaur: https://chatgpt.com/share/671a0076-cc20-8013-8e14-b50ae232a6ac
24/10/24, 1:51โฏpm - Gurleen Kaur: class Solution {
    public List<List<Integer>> generate(int numRows) {
     List<List<Integer>> res=new ArrayList<List<Integer>>();
     List<Integer> rowpre=null;
     for(int i=0;i<numRows;++i){
List<Integer> row=new ArrayList<Integer>();
for(int j=0;j<=i;++j){
    if(j==0 ||j==i){
        row.add(1);
    }
    else{
        row.add(rowpre.get(j-1)+rowpre.get(j));
    }
}
 rowpre=row;
 res.add(row);
     }
     return res;
                    }
    }

26/10/24, 5:45โฏpm - Guneet Kaur: Java provides several **advanced data structures** similar to **List of Lists of ArrayLists** to handle complex data. These structures use nested or multi-level collections to model data in a **hierarchical or relational way**. Here are **other similar types** you can explore:

---

## 1. **Array of ArrayLists**
A **fixed-size array** where each element is an `ArrayList`. Useful when you know the number of lists in advance but need flexibility in the size of each inner list.

### **Declaration and Example:**
```java
ArrayList<Integer>[] arrayOfLists = new ArrayList[3];
for (int i = 0; i < 3; i++) {
    arrayOfLists[i] = new ArrayList<>(List.of(i + 1, i + 2));
}
System.out.println(Arrays.toString(arrayOfLists)); // Output: [[1, 2], [2, 3], [3, 4]]
```

### **Use Case:**  
When you need **a fixed number of variable-sized lists**.

---

## 2. **HashMap with List Values**  
A **`HashMap<K, List<V>>`** maps keys to lists of values. This is useful when you need to group elements by a specific key or category.

### **Declaration and Example:**
```java
Map<String, List<String>> studentsByClass = new HashMap<>();
studentsByClass.put("Class A", new ArrayList<>(List.of("Alice", "Bob")));
studentsByClass.put("Class B", new ArrayList<>(List.of("Charlie", "David")));

System.out.println(studentsByClass);  // Output: {Class A=[Alice, Bob], Class B=[Charlie, David]}
```

### **Use Case:**  
When you need to **group elements** under specific keys (e.g., students by class, products by category).

---

## 3. **List of Maps**  
A **`List<Map<K, V>>`** contains multiple maps, each with key-value pairs. This is useful when you need to store a collection of maps, such as configuration settings or JSON-like data.

### **Declaration and Example:**
```java
List<Map<String, String>> userProfiles = new ArrayList<>();

Map<String, String> user1 = new HashMap<>();
user1.put("name", "Alice");
user1.put("email", "alice@example.com");

Map<String, String> user2 = new HashMap<>();
user2.put("name", "Bob");
user2.put("email", "bob@example.com");

userProfiles.add(user1);
userProfiles.add(user2);

System.out.println(userProfiles);  // Output: [{name=Alice, email=alice@example.com}, {name=Bob, email=bob@example.com}]
```

### **Use Case:**  
When you need a **collection of independent maps**, such as user profiles or configuration settings.

---

## 4. **Set of Lists (Set<List<E>>)**  
A **`Set<List<E>>`** ensures that no two lists inside the set are identical. This is helpful if you need to maintain **unique lists**.

### **Declaration and Example:**
```java
Set<List<Integer>> setOfLists = new HashSet<>();
setOfLists.add(List.of(1, 2, 3));
setOfLists.add(List.of(4, 5, 6));
setOfLists.add(List.of(1, 2, 3));  // Duplicate, will not be added

System.out.println(setOfLists);  // Output: [[1, 2, 3], [4, 5, 6]]
```

### **Use Case:**  
When you want to store **unique combinations of elements** without duplicates.

---

## 5. **Queue of Lists (Queue<List<E>>)**  
A **`Queue<List<E>>`** holds lists that need to be processed in **FIFO (First-In-First-Out)** order. This is useful for scheduling or batch processing.

### **Declaration and Example:**
```java
Queue<List<Integer>> queueOfLists = new LinkedList<>();
queueOfLists.add(List.of(1, 2, 3));
queueOfLists.add(List.of(4, 5, 6));

System.out.println(queueOfLists.poll());  // Output: [1, 2, 3]
System.out.println(queueOfLists);         // Output: [[4, 5, 6]]
```

### **Use Case:**  
When you need to process **batches of data sequentially**, such as jobs or tasks.

---

## 6. **List of Sets (List<Set<E>>)**  
A **`List<Set<E>>`** contains multiple sets. This is useful when each set needs to maintain **unique elements**, but the order of the sets themselves matters.

### **Declaration and Example:**
```java
List<Set<Integer>> listOfSets = new ArrayList<>();
listOfSets.add(new HashSet<>(Set.of(1, 2, 3)));
listOfSets.add(new HashSet<>(Set.of(4, 5, 6)));

System.out.println(listOfSets);  // Output: [[1, 2, 3], [4, 5, 6]]
```

### **Use Case:**  
When you need **collections with unique elements** but want to maintain the sequence of sets.

---

## 7. **Map of Lists of Lists (Map<K, List<List<E>>>)**  
This complex structure maps keys to **nested lists**. Itโs helpful when you need to group multi-level lists by specific keys.

### **Declaration and Example:**
```java
Map<String, List<List<Integer>>> classGrades = new HashMap<>();

classGrades.put("Class A", List.of(List.of(90, 85), List.of(80, 88)));
classGrades.put("Class B", List.of(List.of(70, 75), List.of(60, 68)));

System.out.println(classGrades);  // Output: {Class A=[[90, 85], [80, 88]], Class B=[[70, 75], [60, 68]]}
```

### **Use Case:**  
When you need to **group multi-level lists** by some key, such as student grades by class.

---

## **Comparison of Structures**

| **Structure**              | **Use Case**                                            | **Example**                                 |
|----------------------------|---------------------------------------------------------|---------------------------------------------|
| Array of ArrayLists         | Fixed number of dynamic lists                          | Dynamic matrix                             |
| HashMap with List Values    | Group elements by key                                  | Students by class                          |
| List of Maps                | Store multiple independent maps                        | User profiles                              |
| Set of Lists                | Unique lists                                           | Unique data combinations                   |
| Queue of Lists              | Batch processing in FIFO order                         | Task scheduling                            |
| List of Sets                | Maintain unique elements inside multiple sets          | Unique student groups                      |
| Map of Lists of Lists       | Group multi-level lists by key                         | Student grades by class                    |

---

## **Conclusion**

These **nested data structures** in Javaโlike **List of Lists of ArrayLists**, **Map of Lists**, and **List of Sets**โoffer powerful ways to handle complex relationships between elements. Choose the structure that best fits your **data model** and access pattern requirements to ensure **efficient storage and retrieval**.

04/11/24, 12:00โฏpm - Guneet Kaur: https://leetcode.com/problems/subarray-sum-equals-k/solutions/803317/java-solution-with-detailed-explanation
04/11/24, 12:02โฏpm - Gurleen Kaur: class Solution {
    public int subarraySum(int[] nums, int k) {
        int count = 0;
        for (int i = 0; i < nums.length; i++) {
            int sum = 0; // Initialize sum for each subarray starting at i
            for (int j = i; j < nums.length; j++) {
                sum += nums[j];
                if (sum == k) {
                    count++;
                }
            }
        }
        return count;
    }
}

08/11/24, 11:49โฏam - Guneet Kaur: import java.util.*;

public class UserMainCode {

    public int surpriseDebate(int input1, int[] input2, int input3) {
     
        Arrays.sort(input2);
        int n = input2.length;
        int minValidRollNumber = Integer.MAX_VALUE;
        boolean validPairFound = false;

        
        for (int i = 0; i < n / 2; i++) {
            int pairSum = input2[i] + input2[n - 1 - i];
            if (pairSum % input3 == 0) {
                validPairFound = true;
                minValidRollNumber = Math.min(minValidRollNumber, input2[i]);
            }
        }

       
        if (n % 2 == 1) {
            int lastStudentRollNumber = input2[n / 2];
            if ((lastStudentRollNumber * 2) % input3 == 0) {
                minValidRollNumber = Math.min(minValidRollNumber, lastStudentRollNumber);
            }
        }

       
        if (validPairFound || (n % 2 == 1 && (input2[n / 2] * 2) % input3 == 0)) {
            return minValidRollNumber;
        } else {
            return -1;
        }
    }

08/11/24, 12:20โฏpm - Gurleen Kaur: import java.util.*;

// Read only region start

class UserMainCode {
    public int findCommas(int input1) {
        // Read only region end

        int totalCommas = 0;

        for (int i = 1; i <= input1; i++) {
            totalCommas += countCommasInNumber(i);  // Pass 'i' to the method
        }

        return totalCommas;
    }

    private static int countCommasInNumber(int num) {
        String numStr = Integer.toString(num);
        int length = numStr.length();

        if (length <= 3) {
            return 0;  // No commas needed for numbers with 3 or fewer digits
        }

        return (length - 1) / 3;  // Calculate the number of commas based on the number's length
    }
}

08/11/24, 12:29โฏpm - Gurleen Kaur: import java.util.*;

public class RacingCompetition {

    static class Node {
        int city;
        double time;
        double speed;
        List<Integer> path;

        Node(int city, double time, double speed, List<Integer> path) {
            this.city = city;
            this.time = time;
            this.speed = speed;
            this.path = new ArrayList<>(path);
        }
    }

    public int[] needForSpeed(int input1, String[] input2, int input3, int[][] input4) {
        // Number of cities
        int N = input1;
        // Special powers associated with each city
        String[] specialPowers = input2;
        // Number of routes
        int R = input3;
        // 2D array representing the routes between cities
        int[][] routes = input4;

        // Construct the graph
        Map<Integer, List<Integer>> graph = new HashMap<>();
        for (int i = 0; i < R; i++) {
            int from = routes[i][0];
            int to = routes[i][1];
            graph.computeIfAbsent(from, k -> new ArrayList<>()).add(to);
        }

        // Priority queue to keep track of the minimum time paths
        PriorityQueue<Node> pq = new PriorityQueue<>(Comparator.comparingDouble(node -> node.time));
        pq.offer(new Node(0, 0, 1, Arrays.asList(0)));  // Start at city 0 with 1x speed

        boolean[] visited = new boolean[N];
        while (!pq.isEmpty()) {
            Node current = pq.poll();
            int city = current.city;

            if (visited[city]) continue;
            visited[city] = true;

            // If we reach the destination city (N-1)
            if (city == N - 1) {
                int[] resultPath = current.path.stream().mapToInt(i -> i).toArray();
                return resultPath;
            }

            // Traverse all connected cities
            if (graph.containsKey(city)) {
                for (int nextCity : graph.get(city)) {
                    if (visited[nextCity]) continue;

                    double newSpeed = current.speed;
                    double newTime = current.time + 1 / newSpeed;
                    List<Integer> newPath = new ArrayList<>(current.path);
                    newPath.add(nextCity);

                    // Handle special powers
                    switch (specialPowers[nextCity].toUpperCase()) {
                        case "NITRO":
                            newSpeed *= 2; // Double speed for the next two routes
                            break;
                        case "SAND":
                            newSpeed /= 2; // Halve speed for the next two routes
                            break;
                        case "CRASH":
                            newTime += 1; // Additional 1 hour due to crash
                            break;
                        case "COP":
                            continue; // Skip this path as we get arrested
                    }

                    pq.offer(new Node(nextCity, newTime, newSpeed, newPath));
                }
            }
        }

        // No path found
        return new int[]{-1};
    }

    public static void main(String[] args) {
        RacingCompetition competition = new RacingCompetition();
        int input1 = 5; // Number of cities
        String[] input2 = {"None", "Cop", "None", "None", "None"}; // Special powers
        int input3 = 5; // Number of routes
        int[][] input4 = {
            {0, 1}, {0, 2}, {1, 2}, {2, 3}, {3, 4}
        }; // Routes

        int[] result = competition.needForSpeed(input1, input2, input3, input4);
        System.out.println(Arrays.toString(result));
    }
}

10/12/24, 12:49โฏam - Gurleen Kaur: import requests

def get_chatbot_response(prompt, context):
    """
    Get response from Hugging Face Inference API
    """
    api_url = "https://api-inference.huggingface.co/models/gpt2"
    headers = {"Authorization": "Bearer YOUR_HUGGING_FACE_API_TOKEN"}

    try:
        payload = {
            "inputs": f"Context: {context}\n\nUser: {prompt}\nBot:",
            "options": {"wait_for_model": True},
        }
        response = requests.post(api_url, headers=headers, json=payload)
        response.raise_for_status()
        return response.json()["generated_text"]
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"Error with Hugging Face API: {str(e)}")
        return None

10/12/24, 1:00โฏam - Gurleen Kaur: import os
import requests
from bs4 import BeautifulSoup
import openai
import time

def print_welcome():
    """Print welcome message and instructions"""
    print("=" * 50)
    print("Welcome to the BotPenguin Website Chatbot!")
    print("=" * 50)
    print("\nThis chatbot runs in your terminal/console and can answer")
    print("questions about the content from botpenguin.com")
    print("\nHow it works:")
    print("1. The bot will first scrape content from botpenguin.com")
    print("2. You can then type your questions about BotPenguin")
    print("3. The bot will respond using AI to answer your questions")
    print("\nCommands:")
    print("- Type your question and press Enter to get an answer")
    print("- Type 'quit' to exit the program")
    print("=" * 50)

def scrape_website(url):
    """
    Scrape content from the given website URL
    """
    print("\nConnecting to botpenguin.com...")
    try:
        response = requests.get(url)
        response.raise_for_status()
        soup = BeautifulSoup(response.text, 'html.parser')
        
        # Extract text content from relevant tags
        text_content = []
        for tag in soup.find_all(['p', 'h1', 'h2', 'h3', 'h4', 'h5', 'h6']):
            if tag.text.strip():
                text_content.append(tag.text.strip())
        
        print("Successfully retrieved website content!")
        return ' '.join(text_content)
    except requests.exceptions.ConnectionError:
        print("Error: Could not connect to the website. Please check your internet connection.")
        return None
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"Error scraping website: {str(e)}")
        return None

def get_chatbot_response(prompt, context):
    """
    Get response from ChatGPT API
    """
    try:
        # Set your API key
        openai.api_key = "YOUR_API_KEY"  # Replace with your OpenAI API key
        
        print("Generating response...")
        response = openai.ChatCompletion.create(
            model="gpt-3.5-turbo",
            messages=[
                {"role": "system", "content": f"You are a helpful chatbot that answers questions about BotPenguin based on this content: {context}. Keep responses concise and relevant."},
                {"role": "user", "content": prompt}
            ]
        )
        return response['choices'][0]['message']['content']
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"Error with ChatGPT API: {str(e)}")
        return None

def main():
    """Main function to run the chatbot"""
    print_welcome()
    
    # URL of the website to scrape
    url = "https://botpenguin.com/"
    
    # Scrape website content
    website_content = scrape_website(url)
    
    if not website_content:
        print("\nFailed to initialize the chatbot. Please try again later.")
        return

    print("\nChatbot is ready! You can start asking questions.")
    print("Type 'quit' to exit the program.\n")

    # Main conversation loop
    while True:
        try:
            user_input = input("\nYour question: ").strip()
            
            if user_input.lower() == 'quit':
                print("\nThank you for using the BotPenguin Chatbot. Goodbye!")
                break
            
            if not user_input:
                print("Please type a question!")
                continue
            
            # Get and display the response
            response = get_chatbot_response(user_input, website_content)
            if response:
                print("\nBot:", response)
            else:
                print("\nSorry, I couldn't generate a response at the moment. Please try again.")
                
        except KeyboardInterrupt:
            print("\n\nExiting the chatbot. Goodbye!")
            break
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"\nAn error occurred: {str(e)}")
            print("Please try again.")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    try:
        main()
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"\nCritical error: {str(e)}")
        print("The chatbot has encountered an error and needs to close.")

Open Visual Studio Code.

2. Ensure Python is Installed

Copy code

3. Install Required Python Libraries
Before running the script, ensure you have the required libraries installed. Open a terminal in VS Code (or Command Prompt) and run:

bash
Copy code

bash
Copy code

Copy code

bash
Copy code

5. Run the Script in Command Prompt

bash
Copy code
cd path\to\your\script
Run the script:
bash
Copy code
python chatbot.py
6. Interact with the Chatbot
Once the script is running:

Follow the on-screen instructions.
Ask questions about the content from BotPenguin or type quit to exit.
7. Troubleshooting
If python doesn't work, try python3 instead.
If the terminal shows a module not found error, ensure all dependencies (requests, beautifulsoup4, openai) are installed properly using pip install.
If the chatbot fails to generate responses, check:
The validity of your OpenAI API key.
Network connectivity.
